class="article__primary-category__link gradient-text gradient-text--green-gradient" href="https://techcrunch.com/category/apps/">Apps</a></div><h1 class="article__title">X is launching two new subscription tiers, including a ‘Premium+’ ad-free plan</h1></div><div class="article__byline-wrapper"><div class="article__byline"><a rel="" aria-label="Posts by Aisha Malik" href="https://techcrunch.com/author/aisha-malik/">Aisha Malik</a><span class="article__byline__meta"><a href="https://twitter.com/aiishamalik1">@aiishamalik1</a><span class="article__byline__meta__slash"> / </span><time class="full-date-time" datetime="2023-10-27T19:30:50">3:30 AM GMT+8<span class="full-date-time__separator">•</span>October 28, 2023</time></span></div><div class="container__access-control"><div class="article__action-links"><div class="article__action-links__comments"><button type="button"><svg class="icon icon--comment icon--green-gradient" viewBox="0 0 20 20" version="1.1" aria-labelledby="title"><title>comment</title><path d="M15.3,14.1h2.4v2.4h-2.4V14.1z M12.5,11.8H0v2.4h15.3v-2.4H12.5z class="article__action-links__label">Comment</span></button></div></div></div></div></header></div><div class="article__content-wrap"><img alt="X (formerly Twitter) logo on a cracked wall" class="article__featured-image article__featured-image--block" sizes="(max-width: 730px) 100vw, (max-width: 1600px) 75vw, 1390px" src="./web_files/twitter-x-logo-musk-2.jpg" srcset="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/twitter-x-logo-musk-2.jpg?w=400&amp;crop=1 400w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/twitter-x-logo-musk-2.jpg?w=730&amp;crop=1 1390w"><div class="image-credits"><p><svg class="icon icon--camera icon--green-gradient" viewBox="0 0 20 20" version="1.1" aria-labelledby="title"><title>camera</title><path d="M1,5H19V16.91H1ZM12,3h4V5H12ZM10,13.27a2.32,2.32,0,0,1,0-4.64h0a2.32,2.32,0,0,1,0,4.64Z"></path></svg><strong>Image Credits: </strong>TechCrunch</p></div><div class="article-content"><p id="speakable-summary">X, formerly known as Twitter, is introducing <a href="https://twitter.com/premium/status/1717977644996644948" target="_blank" rel="noopener">two new tiers</a> for its subscription offering in order to bring in additional revenue. The social media giant is adding a new Premium+ tier that costs $16 per month and offers the “largest reply boost” and removes ads from the For You and Following feeds. The tier also comes with revenue-sharing, along with access to other creator tools.</p><p>The second tier launching today is called “Basic” and costs $3 per month. The tier doesn’t come with a blue checkmark, but includes basic features like the ability to edit posts and post longer text and videos. It also offers a “small reply boost.”</p><div class="embed breakout embed-oembed embed--twitter"><div class="twitter-tweet twitter-tweet-rendered" style="display: flex; max-width: 550px; width: 100%; margin-top: 10px; margin-bottom: 10px;"><iframe id="twitter-widget-3" scrolling="no" frameborder="0" allowtransparency="true" allowfullscreen="true" class="" style="position: static; visibility: visible; width: 550px; height: 441px; display: block; flex-grow: 1;" title="X Post" src="./web_files/Tweet.html" data-tweet-id="1717977644996644948"></iframe></div><div class="piano-inline-promo"><div class="tp-container-inner" style="height: 238px; width: 1044.75px;"><iframe id="offer_fc7f02d4e07c4c74d0b1-2" name="offer_fc7f02d4e07c4c74d0b1-2" title="offer_fc7f02d4e07c4c74d0b1-2" scrolling="no" allowtransparency="true" allow="payment" allowfullscreen="true" src="./web_files/cacheableShow.html" frameborder="0" style="overflow: hidden; background-color: transparent; border: 0px; width: 1044.75px; height: 238px;"></iframe></div></div><p></p></div><p>Both of the new tiers are now available on the web.</p><div class="container__access-control"><div class="ad-unit  "><div style="margin-bottom: 0px;"><div class="ad-unit__ad ad-unit__us_tc_ros_dt_native_midarticle" id="tc-ad-tc-target-mid-article-2621261"></div></div></div></div><p>The new tiers join the standard X Premium tier, which replaced Twitter Blue. The tier costs $8 per month and gives users a blue checkmark, prioritized ranking in replies, bookmark folders, longer posts, text formatting, themes, sms two-factor authentication, encrypted DMs and more.</p><p>The launch of the new tiers comes<a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/06/x-to-test-three-tiers-of-its-premium-service-ceo-says-code-shows-one-tier-may-be-ad-free/"> a few weeks</a> after <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2023-10-05/x-tells-bankers-that-advertisers-are-back-but-spending-less?sref=gni836kR" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Bloomberg</a> reported that X was working on new subscription tiers.</p><p>The introduction of the new tiers will give X additional ways to grow revenues as it deals with the loss in advertising dollars that it has faced since Elon Musk took the reins of the platform last fall. Musk’s controversial changes have turned away advertisers, as major companies ended up pulling their ads from the social network after their ads were displayed next to hate speech <a href="https://fortune.com/2023/08/17/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mrf-link="https://fortune.com/2023/08/17/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups/">and pro-Nazi content.</a> Earlier this month, <a href="https://www.reuters.com/technology/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04/" target="_blank" rel="noopener" data-mrf-link="https://www.reuters.com/technology/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04/">Reuters</a> reported that the company’s U.S. ad revenue has declined every month since Musk took over, with the latest figures showing a 60% year-over-year decline as of August.</p><p>Since taking over the company last year, Musk has been looking for ways to generate additional revenue, and has gone so far as charging users in New Zealand and the Philippines <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/17/x-starts-experimenting-with-a-1-per-year-fee-for-new-users">$1 per year</a> in order to access the social network.</p><div class="embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch"><blockquote class="wp-embedded-content" data-secret="w3xp4u7QHX" style="display: none;"><p><a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/27/a-year-after-musks-takeover-x-says-an-average-user-spends-32-minutes-per-day-on-the-platform/">A year after Musk’s takeover, X says an average user spends 32 minutes per day on the platform</a></p></blockquote><p><iframe class="wp-embedded-content" sandbox="allow-scripts" security="restricted" title="“A year after Musk’s takeover, X says an average user spends 32 minutes per day on the platform” — TechCrunch" src="./web_files/saved_resource.html" data-secret="w3xp4u7QHX" width="800" height="261" frameborder="0" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" scrolling="no"></iframe></p></div></div><div id="piano-recirculation-article-footer"></div><div class="container__access-control"><div class="article__comments"><div ad-unit__us_tc_ros_dt_btm_center" id="tc-ad-footer-article-2621261"></div></div></div></div><article class="post-block post-block--image post-block--unread post-block--hidden"><header class="post-block__header"><div class="article__primary-category"><a class="article__primary-category__link gradient-text gradient-text--green-gradient" href="https://techcrunch.com/category/apps/">Apps</a></div><h2 class="post-block__title"><a class="post-block__title__link" href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/27/x-is-launching-new-premium-and-basic-subscription-tiers/">X is launching two new subscription tiers, including a ‘Premium+’ ad-free plan</a></h2><div class="post-block__meta"><div class="river-byline"><span class="river-byline__authors"><span><a rel="" aria-label="Posts by Aisha Malik" href="https://techcrunch.com/author/aisha-malik/">Aisha Malik</a></span></span><div class="river-byline__full-date-time__wrapper"><time class="river-byline__full-date-time" datetime="2023-10-27T19:30:50">3:30 AM GMT+8<span class="full-date-time__separator">•</span>October 28, 2023</time></div></div></div></header><div class="post-block__content">X, formerly known as Twitter, is introducing two new tiers for its subscription offering in order to bring in additional revenue. They don\u2019t all burn so brightly and explode so spectacularly. More often than not, there won\u2019t be some high-profile court case and prison time. Amanda Seyfried isn\u2019t going to play you in the made for Hulu movie.<\/p>\n<p>The story of most startup failures is far less exciting. The timing isn\u2019t right, funding dries up, runways run out. Of late, a lot of macroeconomic factors have come into play, as well. These past few years have been especially brutal for startup land. According to a recent <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2023\/12\/07\/technology\/tech-startups-collapse.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">PitchBook survey,<\/a> \u201capproximately 3,200 private venture-backed U.S. companies have gone out of business this year.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Combined, those companies raised north of $27 billion. Even more starkly, it\u2019s a figure that doesn\u2019t include companies that failed after going public or were able to find a buyer. That, after all, would really be stretching the definition of a \u201cstartup.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s worth noting, too, that \u201cfailure\u201d is subjective. Does bankruptcy qualify? It\u2019s certainly not a good sign with regard to your company\u2019s health, but plenty of companies have managed to bounce back to some degree. This particular question has been cause for plenty of discussion around the old TechCrunch virtual watercooler.<\/p>\n<p>For the sake of a piece titled \u201cThe Startups We Lost,\u201d I\u2019ve opted to limit the list to those startups that &#8212; to the best of our knowledge &#8212; have hit the point of no return. Pushing up daisies. Pining for the fjords.<\/p>\n<p>As the final days fall off the calendar, let\u2019s take a moment to remember some of the startups that didn\u2019t make it.<\/p>\n<h2>Braid<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2019<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$10 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2299903\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2299903\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2299903\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"682\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png 1801w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=1536,1023 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/Braid-Pool.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2299903\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Braid<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In October,\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/13\/braid-group-wallet-to-share-money-with-friends\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/13\/braid-group-wallet-to-share-money-with-friends\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Braid<\/a>, a four-year-old startup that aimed to make shared wallets more mainstream among consumers, announced it had\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/09\/consumer-payments-startup-braid-shuts-down-cites-struggles-with-leveraging-third-party-software\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/09\/consumer-payments-startup-braid-shuts-down-cites-struggles-with-leveraging-third-party-software\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">shut down<\/a>. Founded in January 2019 by Amanda Peyton and Todd Berman (who left in 2020), San Francisco-based Braid set out to offer friends and family an FDIC-insured, multiuser account that was designed to make it easy \u201cto pool, manage and spend money together.\u201d Braid raised a total of $10 million in funding \u201cover multiple rounds\u201d from Index Ventures, Accel and others.<\/p>\n<p>What was refreshing about this closure was Peyton\u2019s candor about what led to Braid\u2019s demise. In\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/amandapeyton.com\/blog\/2023\/10\/braid-is-dead-long-live-braid\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/amandapeyton.com\/blog\/2023\/10\/braid-is-dead-long-live-braid\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">a blog post<\/a>, Peyton said that Braid had closed its doors in September, and outlined her experiences &#8212; and mistakes &#8212; in building the company, ultimately realizing that it wasn\u2019t going to be a viable business venture. An estimated 91% of startups fail. If more founders shared their experience like Peyton did so others could learn from them, maybe that number would go down.<\/p>\n<h2>CloudNordic<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2007<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646327\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646327\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2646327\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg\" alt=\"a screenshot of CloudNordic's status page that reads, &quot;Unfortunately, it has proved impossible to recreate more data, and the majority of our customers have thus lost all data with us.&quot;\" width=\"1024\" height=\"500\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg 1084w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg?resize=150,73 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg?resize=300,146 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg?resize=768,375 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg?resize=680,332 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/cloudnordic-azero-shut-down.jpg?resize=50,24 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646327\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch (screenshot)<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>CloudNordic might not be a household name, but a destructive ransomware attack on its systems propelled the company into the limelight \u2014 and its ultimate demise. The Danish cloud host provider shut down this year after close to two decades of operation <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/23\/cloudnordic-azero-cloud-host-ransomware\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">following a ransomware attack that wiped out the company&#8217;s systems and destroyed all of its customers&#8217; data<\/a>. The company said it didn&#8217;t have the money to pay the hackers, and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/31\/ransomware-victims-paying-hackers-ransom\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wouldn&#8217;t even if it did<\/a>. With no options left, the company closed its doors.<\/p>\n<h2>Convoy<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2015<\/em><br \/>\n<em>More than $1 billion raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1911346\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1911346\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1911346\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg\" alt=\"Convoy trucking\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg 6720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/ConvoyTrailers2019.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-1911346\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Convoy<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The digital freight broker <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/22\/tesla-digs-its-own-grave-with-the-cybertruck-convoy-collapses-and-rivian-scores-a-win-at-rebelle\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">abruptly closed<\/a> in October 2023, just eight months after the Seattle-based company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/convoy-raises-260m-series-e-to-expand-digital-freight-network-products\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">raised $260 million<\/a> in fresh funding that pushed its valuation to $3.8 billion. Convoy, founded by former Amazon and Google exec CEO Dan Lewis and CTO Grant Goodale, will live on \u2014 sort of.<\/p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Supply chain logistics platform <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/01\/flexport-acquires-technology-of-former-digital-freight-unicorn-convoy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Flexport acquired the assets<\/a> of the shuttered digital freight network with plans to\u00a0restore Convoy\u2019s trucking logistics services for customers. Flexport didn&#8217;t acquire the business or any of its liabilities, but its CEO said it did plan to retain \u201ca small group of team members from their core product and engineering team.\u201d<\/p>\n<h2>Daylight<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2020<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$20 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2547436\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2547436\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2547436\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"513\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg?resize=150,75 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg?resize=300,150 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg?resize=768,385 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg?resize=680,341 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/05\/Daylight.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2547436\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Daylight<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In May 2023,\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/daylight\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/daylight\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Daylight<\/a>, an LGBTQ+ banking platform that had raised $20 million in funding, announced it would be\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/22\/daylight-the-lgbtq-neobank-calls-it-quits\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/22\/daylight-the-lgbtq-neobank-calls-it-quits\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">shutting down<\/a> and ceasing operations on June 30. The announcement came months after NY Magazine published an explosive feature on the neobank. The <a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/nymag.com\/intelligencer\/article\/daylight-financial-banking-lawsuit.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/nymag.com\/intelligencer\/article\/daylight-financial-banking-lawsuit.html\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">article<\/a>\u00a0honed in on Daylight, whose seed and Series A fundraises TechCrunch had covered\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/30\/daylight-raises-millions-to-build-a-digital-banking-platform-designed-for-and-by-the-lgbtq-community\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/30\/daylight-raises-millions-to-build-a-digital-banking-platform-designed-for-and-by-the-lgbtq-community\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">here<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/11\/18\/daylight-queer-neobank-raises-15m-capital-subscription-service\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/11\/18\/daylight-queer-neobank-raises-15m-capital-subscription-service\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">here<\/a>, respectively. NY Mag\u2019s piece detailed a lawsuit brought on by three former employees as well as alleged fabrications and inappropriate behavior on the part of co-founder and CEO Rob Curtis.<\/p>\n<p>In a<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/medium.com\/@rob_30313\/reflections-on-closing-daylight-4c8eaa48f37d\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/medium.com\/@rob_30313\/reflections-on-closing-daylight-4c8eaa48f37d\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">\u00a0blog<\/a> published in May, Curtis said he felt like \u201cnow is the right time to exit this market.\u201d We heard in October that the suits had been dismissed by a federal court and that Daylight was acquired, but Curtis declined to comment further when we reached out. It was a disappointing outcome but one that highlighted the challenges of neobanks that target specific demographics. At the onset of the COVID-19 pandemic, we saw a flurry of such startups raising money, but since then, things have been relatively quiet. Part of the challenge is providing differentiated services that are actually unique to a certain community. Since Daylight\u2019s closure, Curtis has moved on to a tequila-related venture.<\/p>\n<h2>Fuzzy<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2016<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$80 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2237395\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2237395\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2237395\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"463\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png 1872w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=150,68 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=300,136 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=768,347 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=680,308 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=1536,695 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=1200,543 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/11\/Fuzzy-Puppy.png?resize=50,23 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2237395\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Fuzzy<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Some startups die long, protracted deaths. Not Fuzzy. The pet care telehealth startup was here one day and gone the next. In February, the firm was <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sfgate.com\/tech\/article\/san-francisco-pet-startup-fuzzy-shuts-down-18161874.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reportedly<\/a> hyping its growth on internal Zoom calls. Within months, the company had closed up shop. Fuzzy\u2019s site was taken down without any warning issued to customers.<\/p>\n<p>From the sound of things, even some top execs were <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:7075884350810046464\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">left wondering<\/a> precisely what had happened to the startup. That certainly hasn\u2019t stopped the competition from attempting to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.dutch.com\/blogs\/general\/fuzzy-shuts-down#one\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">capitalize<\/a> on Fuzzy\u2019s demise.<\/p>\n<h2>IRL<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2016<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$200 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2165858\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2165858\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2165858\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg\" alt=\"irl logo\" width=\"1024\" height=\"653\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg 1390w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=150,96 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=300,191 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=768,490 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=680,433 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=1200,765 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/06\/irl-logo.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2165858\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> IRL<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>IRL\u2019s meltdown was a hot mess. In 2022, the event organizing social app laid off one-quarter of its 100 or so employees. Co-founder and CEO Abraham Shafi put the blame on an extremely volatile market, while stating that the company\u2019s cash runway would last at least until 2024. Then it shut down <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/26\/irl-shut-down-fake-users\/\">this June<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>No social network is completely devoid of bots, but an internal investigation by its board of directors found that such accounts constituted around 95% of its 20 million active monthly users. In a lawsuit filed <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/16\/irl-founders-allege-investors-sabotaged-company-with-fake-users-claims\/\">last month<\/a>, IRL\u2019s co-founders accused their investors of falsifying that figure in order to sabotage the firm, which was previously valued at $1.17 billion.<\/p>\n<h2>IronNet<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2014 <\/em><br \/>\n<em>$400 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646317\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646317\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2646317 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg\" alt=\"Keith Alexander on stage speaking to Matt Burns at TechCrunch Disrupt in 2017\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg 1995w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=1536,1025 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=1200,801 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/keith-alexander-disrupt-ironnet-getty.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646317\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">IronNet founder Keith Alexander at TechCrunch Disrupt in 2017. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Noam Galai \/ Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>IronNet, founded by former NSA director Keith Alexander, was a once-promising cybersecurity startup, which at its peak raised more than $400 million in funding. But in the end, IronNet was no match for market forces (and poor leadership). After <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/06\/29\/cybersecurity-startups-layoffs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a bumpy ride going public and rounds of layoffs<\/a>, Alexander departed as CEO in July and was replaced with the chairperson of the company&#8217;s largest investor. IronNet scrambled to stay afloat, but lasted only a few weeks longer <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/02\/ironnet-founded-by-former-nsa-director-shuts-down-and-lays-off-staff\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">before it laid off everyone else and filed for bankruptcy<\/a>.<\/p>\n<h2>Mandolin<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2020<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$17 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2358046\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2358046\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2358046\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"518\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png 2846w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=150,76 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=300,152 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=768,389 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=680,344 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=1536,777 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=2048,1036 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=1200,607 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/07\/Screen-Shot-2022-07-21-at-10.24.16-AM.png?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2358046\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> <a href=\"https:\/\/mandol.ink\/ben-folds\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mandolin <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Plenty of startups struggled through the pandemic. Others thrived. Founded in June 2020, the concert livestreaming platform was the right startup at the right time. After all, it had only been a few months since venues across the U.S. closed their doors indefinitely. Mandolin\u2019s subsequent rise was swift, taking on big name events with artists ranging from Lil\u2019 Wayne to the Lumineers.<\/p>\n<p>A year after its founding, the Indianapolis-based firm <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/30\/concert-livestreaming-platform-mandolin-raises-12m\/\">raised a $12 million Series A<\/a>, following a $5 million seed round the previous October. In 2022, it seemed as though the platform was still thriving, even as venues across the country had re-opened. Mandolin diversified into other aspects of the live music experience, including venue partnerships and merchandizing.<\/p>\n<p>This April, however, the startup announced on Instagram that it was closing up shop. \u201cAfter 3 incredible years,\u201d it noted, \u201cwe are sad to announce that Mandolin will no longer be offering the digital fan experiences you\u2019ve come to love.\u201d<\/p>\n<h2>Veev<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2008<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$597 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2277919\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2277919\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2277919\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg\" alt=\"Veev raises $400M\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1040-Laurel-St-San-Carlos-07-of-58-1-1.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2277919\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Veev<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Veev, a real estate developer turned tech-enabled prefab homebuilder, as of November was on the verge of\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/27\/prefab-home-builder-veev-reportedly-shutting-down-after-reaching-unicorn-status-last-year\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/27\/prefab-home-builder-veev-reportedly-shutting-down-after-reaching-unicorn-status-last-year\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">shuttering<\/a>\u00a0after\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/real-estate-developer-turned-prefab-home-builder-veev-closes-on-400m-in-funding\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/real-estate-developer-turned-prefab-home-builder-veev-closes-on-400m-in-funding\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">reaching unicorn status last year<\/a>, according to multiple reports. Calcalist <a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/www.calcalistech.com\/ctechnews\/article\/s1g004ylr6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/www.calcalistech.com\/ctechnews\/article\/s1g004ylr6\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">reported<\/a>\u00a0on November 26 that the company \u2014 which raised a staggering $600 million in total,\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/real-estate-developer-turned-prefab-home-builder-veev-closes-on-400m-in-funding\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/real-estate-developer-turned-prefab-home-builder-veev-closes-on-400m-in-funding\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">$400 million of which was secured<\/a>\u00a0in March of 2022 \u2014 was going to have to close up shop after an \u201cabrupt cancellation of a capital-raising initiative.\u201d Later that week, it was reported that Veev was \u201c<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/www.builderonline.com\/money\/capital\/explainer-why-did-veev-fail-and-what-happens-next_o\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/www.builderonline.com\/money\/capital\/explainer-why-did-veev-fail-and-what-happens-next_o\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">undergoing liquidation<\/a>.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>It was a bit of a shocking turn of events considering just how much money the company had raised not even two years prior. The closure was not the first startup failure for Veev co-founders Heller and Ami Avrahami. Another one of their proptech ventures, Reali, began a shutdown in August of 2022 after\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/08\/25\/real-estate-tech-startup-reali-to-shut-down-after-raising-100m-one-year-ago\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/08\/25\/real-estate-tech-startup-reali-to-shut-down-after-raising-100m-one-year-ago\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">raising more than $290 million in debt and equity funding<\/a>. Zeev Ventures was an investor in both companies.<\/p>\n<h2>ZestMoney<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2015<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$121 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1699921\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1699921\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1699921\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg\" alt=\"ZestMoney founders\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg 1326w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/08\/ZestMoney-Founders.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1699921\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">ZestMoney founders resign as Goldman Sachs-backed fintech struggles to raise funds. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> ZestMoney<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In mid-May, Manish reported on the fact that founders of ZestMoney\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/15\/zestmoney-founders-resign-as-goldman-sachs-backed-fintech-struggles-to-raise-funds\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/15\/zestmoney-founders-resign-as-goldman-sachs-backed-fintech-struggles-to-raise-funds\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">had resigned from the startup<\/a>. The Indian fintech, whose ability to underwrite small ticket loans to first-time internet customers, once drew the backing of many high-profile investors,\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/18\/zestmoney-goldman-sachs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/18\/zestmoney-goldman-sachs\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">including Goldman Sachs<\/a>. By December, Manish had reported that ZestMoney was\u00a0<a class=\"c-link\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/05\/goldman-sachs-backed-zestmoney-once-valued-at-450m-to-shut-down\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/05\/goldman-sachs-backed-zestmoney-once-valued-at-450m-to-shut-down\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">shutting down<\/a>\u00a0following unsuccessful efforts to find a buyer.<\/p>\n<p>The Bengaluru-headquartered startup \u2014 which also identified PayU, Quona, Zip, Omidyar Network and Ribbit Capital among its backers \u2014 employed about 150 people and had raised over $130 million in its eight-year journey.<\/p>\n<h2>Zume<\/h2>\n<p><em>Founded 2015<\/em><br \/>\n<em>$445 million raised<\/em><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1628277\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1628277\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1628277\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/zumeexterior1_preview1.jpeg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1628277\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Zume<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cPizza was our prototype,\u201d co-founder and CEO Alex Garden told <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/04\/25\/zume-looks-to-life-beyond-pizza\/\">me in 2018<\/a>. Three years after its founding, Zume made a major pivot. While it will forever be remembered as the pizza robot startup (that\u2019s a hard identity to shake), the Southern Californian company cast a wider net. First it was exploring non-pizza delivery trucks. Two years later, it pivoted into sustainable food packaging.<\/p>\n<p>Throughout its many lives, one certainly can\u2019t pin Zume\u2019s ultimate demise on a failure to adapt. Nor was it a lack of funding, as the company raised nearly half-a-billion in its eight-year history. That includes a 2018 SoftBank round of $325 million that valued the company at north of two billon.<\/p>\n<p>Zume liquidated its assets in early June.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"pCxnXiO1AV\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/28\/convicts-silicon-valley-2023\/\">The convicts of Silicon Valley, 2023 edition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;The convicts of Silicon Valley, 2023 edition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/28\/convicts-silicon-valley-2023\/embed\/#?secret=u2l1FtppRD#?secret=pCxnXiO1AV\" data-secret=\"pCxnXiO1AV\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Not every startup collapse is an FTX or Theranos. name=search_term_string"}],"inLanguage":"en-US"},{"@type":"Organization","@id":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/#organization","name":"TechCrunch","alternateName":"TC","url":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","inLanguage":"en-US","@id":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/","url":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/tc-logo-2018-square-reverse2x.png?resize=1200,1200","contentUrl":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/04\/tc-logo-2018-square-reverse2x.png?resize=1200,1200","width":1200,"height":1200,"caption":"TechCrunch"},"image":{"@id":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/#\/schema\/logo\/image\/"},"sameAs":["https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/techcrunch","https:\/\/twitter.com\/TechCrunch","https:\/\/mstdn.social\/@TechCrunch","https:\/\/bsky.app\/profile\/techcrunch.bsky.social","https:\/\/www.threads.net\/@techcrunch"]}]}},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449552858"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449552858"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_battlefield?tags=449552858"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449552858"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_unified_video?tags=449552858"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449552858"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2646084,"date":"2023-12-29T17:00:04","date_gmt":"2023-12-30T01:00:04","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2646084"},"modified":"2023-12-29T20:09:17","modified_gmt":"2023-12-30T04:09:17","slug":"india-ev-market-2024","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/29\/india-ev-market-2024\/","title":{"rendered":"How India will navigate EVs in 2024"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">India, a major<\/span> player in the global automotive industry, has started focusing on transitioning to alternative fuels to curb pollution after expanding its consumer and vehicle bases and adding local manufacturing facilities over the past two decades. On this journey, 2024 will be a crucial year, as the country \u2014 the third-largest automotive market \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/08\/indias-top-vcs-face-fresh-obstacles-as-startup-investment-plummets\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">faces challenges to offer accessible growth capital<\/a> to late-stage startups while trying to lure <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/20\/elon-musk-modi-india-tesla-starlink\/fzhjlw_acaaw80n\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Tesla<\/a> and other foreign EV manufacturers to enter its domestic market.<\/p>\n<h2>How EVs fared in 2023<\/h2>\n<p>In 2023, India, the world&#8217;s largest two- and three-wheeler manufacturer, sold almost 24 million vehicles, including commercial and personal four-, three- and two-wheelers, according to the latest data on the government&#8217;s Vahan portal. Of the total number of vehicles registered, more than 1.5 million were EVs, capturing 6.35% of the total base, including 813,000 electric two-wheelers. While the overall growth was nearly 10% from about 22 million vehicles sold in 2022, EV sales grew by close to 47% from 1.03 million EVs sold last year.<\/p>\n<p>This brings the total number of electric vehicle sales in the country to nearly 3.5 million. Two-wheelers accounted for more than 47% of sales, four-wheelers represented about 8% and the rest came from e-rickshaws and three-wheelers.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646087\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646087\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2646087\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg\" alt=\"India EV sales\" width=\"1024\" height=\"519\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg?resize=150,76 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg?resize=300,152 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg?resize=768,389 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg?resize=680,345 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-sales.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646087\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">India&#8217;s EV sales grew from nearly 125,000 in 2020 to over 1.5 million in 2023, per the data provided by Vahan.\u00a0<strong>Image Credits:\u00a0<\/strong>Jagmeet Singh \/ TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>India&#8217;s annual growth in EV sales in 2023 is significant; however, it&#8217;s not as high as in the previous two years, which were over 209% in 2022 and 166% in 2021. One of the reasons for the dip in the sales of EVs is the cut in subsidies given to two-wheeler customers through the $1.38 billion incentive scheme called Faster Adoption and Manufacturing of (Hybrid and) Electric Vehicles, commonly called FAME-II, that came into effect in June and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/05\/india-electric-two-wheeler-scooter-sales\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dropped the monthly sales of electric two-wheelers in the country over 56%<\/a> in that month alone. The sudden drop in electric two-wheeler sales has arguably impacted the country&#8217;s overall EV market, as India is predominantly a two-wheeler market and has limited manufacturers in the electric car segment.<\/p>\n<p>Ravneet S. Phokela, chief business officer of electric two-wheeler startup Ather Energy, told TechCrunch the market took a hit for about three months due to the FAME-II update, though it has rebounded to pre-subsidy change levels as of October.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;From the bounce back, how the rapid growth is going to be remains to be seen, but we expect it to be more gradual than exponential. However, the days of 100% quarter-on-quarter growth are gone,&#8221; he said over a call, adding that the change would help in the medium-term perspective.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;In a way, while the subsidy impacted us in the short term financially, if I just take a macro view, there has actually been a good outcome because now, the market pricing is close to non-subsidy levels, which means the market has gotten used to price levels that we can explore broadly when subsidy goes over,&#8221; Phokela noted.<\/p>\n<p>The subsidy update has also caused consolidation and sudden exits of many small-scale electric two-wheeler brands, including the ones selling rebranded Chinese vehicles. Phokela said that the top four players, namely Ola, TVS Motor, Ather Energy and Bajaj, which combined had around 26% to 27% share about nine months ago (before the government updated FAME-II in May), currently capture about 80% of the total electric two-wheeler market<span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px; -webkit-text-size-adjust: 100%;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Ather Energy sold an average of about 80,000 to 85,000 units this year and expects a similar sales figure for 2024, Phokela said.<\/p>\n<p>Apart from electric two-wheelers, the FAME-II scheme applies to three- and four-wheeler sales to boost EV consumption in the country.<\/p>\n<p>New Delhi has given more than $628 million in subsidies through December 1 under FAME-II on the sale of 1.15 million vehicles, according to the government data <a href=\"https:\/\/pib.gov.in\/PressReleasePage.aspx?PRID=1989854\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">shared<\/a> in the parliament.<\/p>\n<p>EV manufacturers have demanded that the government continue offering subsidies to let the market sustain its growth and expand further to meet the country&#8217;s electrification target to have 30% EV penetration by 2030.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Given that the costs are still not optimized yet for the supply chain, it is important for the government to continue the subsidy for two to three years and taper it down,&#8221; Phokela said.<\/p>\n<p>Industry sources told TechCrunch that market players have requested the government provide predictability in its policies and avoid bringing abrupt changes, such as the case of FAME-II updates, to let them make assumptions and base financial and business planning accordingly.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;A lack of predictability is the biggest killer point for the industry,&#8221; an executive at an electric two-wheeler company stated on the condition anonymity. &#8220;Even if you are saying six months, please tell us that it will be for six months and then turnaround, but don&#8217;t say two years and end in one year.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In addition to FAME-II, the Indian government has offered a $3.11 billion production-linked incentive scheme to attract investments and push domestic manufacturing of automobile and auto components in the country. Indian car manufacturers Tata Motors and Mahindra &amp; Mahindra have emerged as the early beneficiaries of the incentive scheme. The government reported more than $1.43 billion of investments came until the second quarter of the financial year 2023-24 as a result of the scheme.<\/p>\n<p>Tata Motors saw a growth of 63% in EVs and increased EV penetration in its portfolio to 12% this year, a company spokesperson said in a statement to TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>Automobile manufacturers, including Ather Energy and Tata Motors, introduced their new EV models in the country to expand their presence and attract new customers.<\/p>\n<p>Phokela underlined that &#8220;premiumization&#8221; emerged as a notable consumer trend this year, particularly in the Indian electric two-wheeler market. The trend of premium models coming to the market will continue in 2024, he predicted.<\/p>\n<p>All four top electric two-wheeler brands have vehicles between the price range of $1,400 to $1,800, while the traditional internal combustion engine two-wheelers are available at an average price of $1,000.<\/p>\n<p>In the last 12 to 18 months, the electric two-wheeler market also saw growing sales from the tier two and tier three towns. For Ather Energy, Phokela said only 43% of its sales came from tier one cities, while 57% was from tier two and tier three towns \u2014 despite its limited distribution in those regions. The startup is now expanding its distribution to get even higher sales.<\/p>\n<p>Some market observers believe that the growth of electric two-wheeler sales in the developing parts of India is due to hefty electricity subsidies. However, Phokela argued that if that were the reason, there would be a significant growth in the demand for low-end vehicles, not the premium models. People in non-metro cities consider EVs as status validation and a way to show off, he said.<\/p>\n<h2>Commercial use cases as a major investor attraction<\/h2>\n<p>Although top electric two-wheeler manufacturers have so far targeted the personal mobility segment in the Indian market, investors are bullish on the growth of commercial use cases.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;In the next two to three years, the majority of the traction will come from B2B use cases \u2014 whether it is three-wheeler cargo, three-wheeler passenger, eco-mobility, food delivery, hyperlocal delivery, fast\/quick commerce, the use of EVs there is the one that&#8217;s accelerating much faster,&#8221; Kunal Khattar, founder and general partner at Indian VC fund AdvantEdge Founders, told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>He said while the share of commercial vehicles is about 30 million, or 10% of the total number of vehicles on the road in India, they consume almost 70% of the energy of all the vehicles.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646099\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646099\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2646099\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg\" alt=\"electric auto rickshaw in Delhi\" width=\"1024\" height=\"684\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg?resize=768,513 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/electric-auto-rickshaw-delhi-getty.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646099\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Commercial electric vehicles consume a large percentage of energy in India.\u00a0<strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Sanchit Khanna\/Hindustan Times<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;If you&#8217;re in the business of energy, whether it is battery manufacturing or swapping, energy storage or building charging infrastructure, your entire focus should be on B2B,&#8221; he noted.<\/p>\n<p>Sandiip Bhammer, founder and co-managing partner at New York-based climate tech VC fund Green Frontier Capital, told TechCrunch the opportunity to gain faster and more rapid growth in the commercial segment is significantly higher than in the consumer segment.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The economic viability of two-wheeler and three-wheeler segments on the commercial side is much clearer than on the passenger car segment,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p>Investors believe that compared to the consumer segment, the commercial segment is less prone to be impacted by subsidy changes. This is because businesses consider the total cost of ownership rather than the face value of the vehicle they purchase.<\/p>\n<p>Khattar said the B2B segment will be 100% electric in India in the next two to three years, irrespective of whether subsidies and other incentives would be available.<\/p>\n<p>The country <a href=\"https:\/\/pib.gov.in\/PressReleaseIframePage.aspx?PRID=1987804\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">plans to add thousands<\/a> of battery-operated auto-rickshaws and e-buses to electrify public transportation across states in the coming months. Likewise, it <a href=\"https:\/\/pib.gov.in\/PressReleaseIframePage.aspx?PRID=1984097\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">looks to offer EV charging stations<\/a> at various local gas stations.<\/p>\n<h2>Capital flow in the market<\/h2>\n<p>Equity investments in India&#8217;s electric vehicle (EV) market decreased by 52%, from $2.1 billion in 2022 to $1 billion in 2023, according to the data shared with TechCrunch by VC analyst firm Tracxn earlier this month. The number of funding rounds also dropped 62%, from 135 in the previous year to 51. However, EV funding was not as dire as in some top-performing sectors, such as tech, SaaS, agritech and health tech, where equity investments dropped by over 80%.<\/p>\n<p>Bhammer of Green Frontier Capital said the drop in EV funding this year was mainly due to valuations that were too high in many of the existing startups.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;If you look at new companies that are raising capital, they are actually raising capital at a much more reasonable valuation than the older companies doing extension rounds,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646091\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646091\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2646091\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg\" alt=\"India EV funding\" width=\"1024\" height=\"410\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg?resize=150,60 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg?resize=300,120 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg?resize=768,307 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg?resize=680,272 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/india-ev-funding.jpg?resize=50,20 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646091\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">India&#8217;s EV funding declined to $1.5 billion in 2023, per the data provided by Tracxn. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Jagmeet Singh \/ TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Investors are optimistic about the capital flow growth in 2024 but cautious about muted numbers, particularly in the consumer segment, due to FAME-II changes and lack of clarity on subsidy extension.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We need the support of the government, in terms of subsidies and taxes and all of that, because of the fact that we are not mainstream yet,&#8221; Khattar of AdvantEdge Founders said.<\/p>\n<p>One key reason for being hopeful is India&#8217;s growing global presence and becoming a part of the China+1 strategy for most global companies.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;China has now started de-growing. So, India is the beacon of hope in an otherwise pretty dull emerging markets scenario,&#8221; Bhammer said.<\/p>\n<h2>What&#8217;s coming up next?<\/h2>\n<p>While India is still a nascent market for EVs, global EV companies including Tesla and VinFast are also looking to enter the Indian market in the coming months to leverage the size of the world&#8217;s most populous nation. The Indian government is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/business\/autos-transportation\/india-aims-attract-investors-germany-uk-korea-under-new-ev-policy-official-2023-12-28\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">developing a new EV policy<\/a> to attract foreign carmakers to foray into the market alongside supporting domestic players to expand the country&#8217;s electric car base. Incumbents including India&#8217;s top carmaker Maruti Suzuki are also closely observing the ongoing moves by international players to look for the right time to enter the market.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Legacy carmakers are in no hurry. When they launch, they will distribute, and through their distribution, they will be able to start selling numbers as much as, if not more than, existing players,&#8221; an EV investor told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>Companies including Tata Motors, which are already in the EV market with their vehicles, are working to address the current adoption challenges.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Charging infrastructure growth remains the residual barrier for mass adoption of EVs. Tata Motors has initiated open collaboration with key charging players to accelerate the growth of chargers, which will deliver a better experience to the EV buyers,&#8221; the Tata Motors spokesperson said.<\/p>\n<p>Ravi Pandit, co-founder and group chairman of automobile tech company KPIT Technologies, told TechCrunch that software and hardware have become the vehicle&#8217;s core and that trend will continue to grow over time.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Now, the model is changing where instead of there being a lot of computers in a car, there will be a computer and around which there will be a car. That&#8217;s a fundamental shift,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p>Similarly, electric two-wheeler manufacturers and infrastructure providers are working on standardized charging solutions. Ather Energy has already collaborated with Hero to offer interoperability on charging.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We have about 1,400 fast chargers, and Hero Vida has about 500, and we are growing on a monthly basis,&#8221; said Phokela. &#8220;We are in conversations with many other OEMs, and these discussions are at different levels of maturity.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In addition to standardization and interoperability on the charging side, some companies are exploring alternatives to lithium, including sodium-ion-driven technologies and silicon anode.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;What is clear is that you cannot drive revolution in any sector unless you have access to the raw materials that power the industry. So, if China controls the refining capacity of lithium, how would India drive the EV revolution if it has to keep going to China for its batteries,&#8221; Bhammer said.<\/p>\n<p>He mentioned that other incoming updates in the market include vehicle-to-grid and clip-on devices that will be available on a subscription-based model to help users convert an existing two-wheeler from a non-EV to an EV without charging the motor or battery permanently.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"36gMkVi3mg\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/18\/gogoro-india\/\">Why Gogoro picked India as its new go-to market<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Why Gogoro picked India as its new go-to market&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/18\/gogoro-india\/embed\/#?secret=lsqwDZHoTh#?secret=36gMkVi3mg\" data-secret=\"36gMkVi3mg\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>India, a major player in the global automotive industry, has started focusing on transitioning to alternative fuels to curb pollution after expanding its consumer and vehicle bases and adding local manufacturing facilities over the past two decades. On this journey, 2024 will be a crucial year, as the country \u2014 the third-largest automotive market \u2014
