Yearly: The biggest startup stories from 2023"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>Welcome to Startups Weekly. Sign up <\/em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>here<\/em><\/a><em> to get it in your inbox every Friday.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Thank you for subscribing to Startups Weekly. This week, I\u2019m taking my parents to Yosemite to explore the snowy peaks and to see if my car can handle snow. In lieu of a regular Startups Weekly, I figured I\u2019d dive in and give you a reminder of some of the biggest startup stories from 2024 \u2014 both on TechCrunch and our subscription sibling TechCrunch+.<\/p>\n<p>Here are some of the biggest themes that have echoed throughout the startup ecosystem in 2023.<\/p>\n<h2>Crime and punishment<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2441297\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2441297\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2441297\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg\" alt=\"FTX logo broken and on fire\" width=\"1024\" height=\"550\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=300,161 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=768,413 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=680,366 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=1536,826 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=2048,1101 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=1200,645 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/11\/ftx-broken-on-fire.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2441297\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin \/ TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Some of the biggest startup stories on TechCrunch in 2023 were related to the deeds and misdeeds of those in the ecosystem.<\/p>\n<p>By far one of our most-read stories this year was <strong>the murder of Bob Lee<\/strong>, best known as the creator of Cash App and former <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2011\/03\/28\/square-cto\/\">CTO of Square<\/a>. He was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/05\/bob-lee-creator-of-cash-app-and-former-cto-of-square-stabbed-to-death\/\">tragically killed in a stabbing incident in San Francisco<\/a>, in the otherwise usually quiet Financial District. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.rollingstone.com\/culture\/culture-features\/bob-lee-murder-cash-app-what-happened-1234852853\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rolling Stone picked up the story from there<\/a>, digging into who Bob Lee and his alleged murderer were.<\/p>\n<p>The <em>other<\/em> big story was the trial of <strong>Theranos founder and CEO Elizabeth Holmes<\/strong>. She is now serving a prison sentence of 11 years and 3 months after being indicted for wire fraud in a scheme to defraud investors. Theranos, once valued at $10 billion, promised revolutionary blood testing technology but was exposed in 2015 for its nonfunctional technology, which posed health risks to patients. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/30\/elizabeth-holmes-is-now-behind-bars-how-we-got-here\/\">The subsequent unraveling of Theranos led to numerous lawsuits and government investigations<\/a>. The case serves as a stark reminder of the consequences of fraudulent practices and that the &#8220;fake it till you make it&#8221; approach that can be prevalent among startups doesn\u2019t always work out.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The <em>other<\/em>\u00a0big &#8220;hmm, maybe you shouldn\u2019t have done that&#8221; serial story of the year was the<strong> Sam Bankman-Fried trial<\/strong>, which extended over five weeks. It turned out to be a spectacle of evasion and memory lapses. The former CEO of FTX <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/sbfs-trial-is-coming-to-a-close-heres-what-you-missed\/\">faced the jury for several days<\/a>, delivering a testimony that was remarkable mostly for its lack of substance. When cross-examined by prosecutors about his past decisions and actions, Bankman-Fried&#8217;s responses were predominantly &#8220;Yup&#8221; (372 times), &#8220;Not sure&#8221; (117 times), and &#8220;I don\u2019t remember&#8221; (73 times). He was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/sam-bankman-fried-found-guilty-on-all-seven-counts\/\">found guilty on all seven charges of fraud and money laundering<\/a>, and will be sentenced in March 2024. Around the same time, there will likely be <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/10\/another-sbf-trial\/\">a second trial<\/a>, with a bunch of additional charges.<\/p>\n<p>More from the courts and legal systems:<\/p>\n<p><strong>It\u2019s not just the startups .\u00a0.\u00a0. :\u00a0\u00a0<\/strong>Former VC Mike Rothenberg, known for hosting extravagant parties, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/16\/yet-another-former-silicon-valley-darling-is-convicted-of-investor-fraud\/\">convicted on 21 counts last month<\/a>, including for bank fraud, false statements, money laundering, and wire fraud. The conviction brings his journey from a promising entrepreneur, launching a VC firm in 2013, to being a convicted fraudster to a close. He was originally <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/08\/20\/the-sec-has-charged-mike-rothenberg-for-fraud\/\">charged with fraud<\/a> by the SEC in 2018, which resulted him <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/20\/court-rules-mike-rothenberg-must-fork-over-more-than-31-million-to-settle-sec-allegations\/\">having to pay $31 million<\/a>. Sentencing in the fraud case is scheduled for March.<\/p>\n<p><strong>I\u2019m trying to reach you about your extended warranty: <\/strong>The FCC imposed a record $300 million fine on a robocaller operation for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/08\/03\/fcc-fines-robocaller-a-record-300m-after-blocking-billions-of-their-scam-calls\/\">scamming people with fake auto warranty sales<\/a>. This operation made at least 5 billion calls.<\/p>\n<p><strong>The Swiss army knife for hackers: <\/strong>Flipper Zero, a multi-tool hacking device, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/26\/flipper-sales\/\">is on track to achieve $80 million in sales this year<\/a>, a significant increase from its $25 million sales last year. Started in 2020, the device can manipulate various systems like garage openers and RFID card systems.<\/p>\n<h2>The fun and quirky<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2553405\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2553405\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2553405\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg\" alt=\"Apple Vision Pro headset\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg 4464w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=1200,800 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/06\/CMC_6538.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2553405\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Brian Heater<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The world of startups wasn\u2019t just murders, fraud and shenanigans \u2014 some of our most-read stories this year were a lot more lighthearted, thank goodness.<\/p>\n<p>One of the highlights was Apple&#8217;s 31 new emojis \u2014 including a shaking face for when you&#8217;re &#8220;shook&#8221; and a pink heart because, obviously, we need more heart colors. There are even two pushing hands that could mean &#8220;stop&#8221; or &#8220;high five&#8221; \u2014 because interpreting vague hand gestures is what we all needed more of. Want to spam your friends with a moose or a jellyfish? <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/02\/16\/ios-16-4-to-bring-31-new-emoji-including-shaking-face-pink-heart-two-pushing-hands-and-more\/\">Apple had your back this year<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>My other favorites in the more-or-less-quirky-news category:<\/p>\n<p><strong>[very recognizable drum riff]: <\/strong>MindGeek, the owner of adult entertainment sites such as Pornhub, Brazzers, and RedTube, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/03\/16\/pornhub-owner-mindgeek-sold-to-private-equity-firm\/\">was acquired by Canadian private equity firm Ethical Capital Partners<\/a>. The terms of the deal were not disclosed.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Strap this computer to your face: <\/strong>Apple\u2019s new mixed-reality (XR) device made a significant impact with its high-quality hardware and features. It boasts 24 million pixels across two panels and advanced optics. It has brand-new chips to ensure smooth performance without judder or frame drops, with accurate eye tracking and gesture control. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/05\/first-impressions-yes-apple-vision-pro-works-and-yes-its-good\/\">Panzer tried it out<\/a>, and I argued that the<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/06\/apple-vision-pro-startup-opportunity\/\"> device would be a game-changer for startups operating in the space<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>We\u2019re getting a little bored of Elon\u2019s antics: <\/strong>At some point, TechCrunch editor Darrell decided he had enough, and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/01\/the-end-of-elon\/\">penned this piece<\/a> \u2014 concluding that enough is enough.<\/p>\n<h2>The year of AI<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2632079\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2632079\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2632079\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg\" alt=\"An illustration of Sam Altman in front of the OpenAI logo\" width=\"1024\" height=\"580\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=150,85 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=300,170 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=768,435 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=680,385 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=1536,870 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=1200,680 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/Sam-Altman-OpenAI.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2632079\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Darrell Etherington with files from Getty under license<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>There can be little doubt that, above all, for better <em>and<\/em> for worse, 2023 was the year of AI.<\/p>\n<p>OpenAI was on everybody\u2019s lips. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/06\/openai-makes-gpt-4-generally-available\/\">The company made GPT-4 universally available<\/a>, which got everyone hella excited. It also gave <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/03\/23\/openai-connects-chatgpt-to-the-internet\/\">ChatGPT the ability to browse the broader internet<\/a>, which unlocked a world of functionality and excitement.<\/p>\n<p>The darker side of AI got its time in the limelight as well. The advancement of AI porn generators, such as Unstable Diffusion, has <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/21\/as-ai-porn-generators-get-better-the-stakes-raise\/\">raised significant ethical and societal concerns<\/a>. These generators, which have improved in creating more realistic and diverse images, are posing some new risks \u2014 and continues to make the internet more toxic, especially for women (the majority of deepfake pornography targets women and is often used as a tool for harassment). We were also successful in <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/12\/06\/lensa-goes-nsfw\/\">tricking Lensa into generating NSFW content<\/a> by putting crudely photoshopped photos into its source material. In short: <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/08\/24\/deepfakes-for-all-uncensored-ai-art-model-prompts-ethics-questions\/\">maybe deepfakes-for-all is worse than we thought<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Another big AI drama story of the year was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/17\/sam-altman-is-out-as-openais-ceo\/\">Sam Altman getting fired as OpenAI\u2019s CEO<\/a>. We put together a whole <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/29\/a-timeline-of-sam-altmans-firing-from-openai-and-the-fallout\/\">timeline<\/a>, because, goodness, that was quite the saga.<\/p>\n<h2>From the desk of &#8220;didn\u2019t see that coming&#8221;<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2500277\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2500277\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2500277\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg\" alt=\"SVB forces African banks to rethink their bank options\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg 2736w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=1200,675 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/03\/GettyImages-1248159709.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2500277\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Nikolas Liepins\/Anadolu Agency \/ Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>If there\u2019s one thing startups love doing, it\u2019s throwing curveballs. This year was no exception, and here are a handful of the most surprising ones:<\/p>\n<p><strong>A banking collapse:<\/strong> Everything was fine one moment, then suddenly one of the biggest startup banks \u2014 Silicon Valley Bank, or SVB among friends \u2014 took a nosedive. We put together <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/03\/16\/svb-crash-2023-timeline\/\">a timeline of what happened<\/a>, along with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/svb-2023-crash\/\">a wall of coverage and analysis<\/a>. Venture debt was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/17\/venture-debt-svb-investor-survey\/\">one of the big question marks<\/a> post-collapse.<\/p>\n<p><strong>The DPReview saga: <\/strong>DPReview, a renowned digital camera review site, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/03\/21\/amazon-kills-dpreview-the-best-camera-review-site-on-the-web\/\">shut down by Amazon after 25 years of operation<\/a>, before Gear Patrol <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/23\/slow-is-smooth-and-smooth-is-fast\/\">bought the property and revived it<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>That submarine story: <\/strong>OceanGate trying to dip down to the Titanic and imploding in the process was everywhere for a hot moment. A <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/20\/a-whistleblower-raised-safety-concerns-about-oceangates-submersible-in-2018-then-he-was-fired\/\">whistleblower was fired in January 2018<\/a> after presenting a scathing quality-control report on the vessel to OceanGate\u2019s senior management, including founder and CEO Stockton Rush \u2014 who later died onboard the submarine. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/03\/15\/oceangate-plans-an-expedition-to-3d-scan-the-titanic\/\">We originally covered the company back in 2017<\/a> when it first revealed the plans to go 3D-scan the Titanic.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Is it a bird? Is it a balloon?: <\/strong>Pathfinder 1 is an electric airship that&#8217;s giving the Goodyear blimp a run for its money. At 124.5 meters long, it&#8217;s like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/08\/the-worlds-largest-aircraft-breaks-cover-in-silicon-valley\/\">the Hindenburg had a tech-savvy baby with a drone<\/a>. With 12 electric motors and a penchant for helium (significantly safer than its high-explosive, Hindenburg-exploding hydrogen counterpart), it\u2019s set to conquer the skies at a whopping 75 mph\u00a0.\u00a0.\u00a0.\u00a0eventually.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Round after round after round of layoffs:<\/strong>\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/21\/tech-layoffs-2023-list\/\">Woof<\/a>.<\/p>\n<h2>The biggest hits from TC+<\/h2>\n<p>TechCrunch+ is TechCrunch\u2019s subscription service, offering in-depth analysis, exclusive articles, and comprehensive reports on the technology industry, startups, and venture capital. If you\u2019re not a subscriber \u2014 well, you should absolutely subscribe.<\/p>\n<p>My popular <a href=\"http:\/\/haje.pub\/pdt\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pitch Deck Teardown series<\/a> is up to more than 75 sample pitch decks, complete with analysis for what\u2019s working and what ain\u2019t. And, of course, there\u2019s oodles of additional amazing content too. Here\u2019s a handful of stories you may have missed:<\/p>\n<p><strong>From cloud to on-premise: <\/strong>After a decade of cloud transformations, sophisticated enterprises are now developing <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/03\/20\/the-cloud-backlash-has-begun-why-big-data-is-pulling-compute-back-on-premises\/\">hybrid strategies to support critical data science initiatives<\/a>, moving away from exclusive reliance on cloud computing and bringing workloads back to on-premises systems.<\/p>\n<p><strong>The evolution of layoffs:<\/strong> Back in July, we looked at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/11\/tech-layoffs-are-changing\">how the era of tech layoffs was evolving<\/a>, noting that while it was not over, it was losing some of its intensity and was developing into its own unique trend.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Stage appropriate over perfection:<\/strong>\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/02\/19\/stage-appropriate-mvps-investors-founders\/\">Startups should focus<\/a> on creating minimum viable products that are laser-focused on answering specific questions, rather than trying to scale too quickly, wasting resources in the process.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Hey, OpenAI, generate a marketing strategy:<\/strong>\u00a0In this case study, we showed <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/20\/we-tried-using-openai-to-generate-marketing-strategies-and-it-worked\">how using OpenAI for generating marketing strategies<\/a> led to significant improvements in SEO ranking on Google, resulting in a substantial increase in site traffic, domain rating, and backlinks in less than a year.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Build on someone else\u2019s tech and get burned:<\/strong> An update on OpenAI&#8217;s ChatGPT allowed for PDF uploads. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/06\/get-the-pdf-outta-here\">That was a spanner in the work for startups<\/a>, especially those built around a feature gap in ChatGPT. It underscored the vulnerability of such businesses to changes in underlying technologies.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Growth is hard:<\/strong> The former CEO of PlanGrid <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/01\/04\/5-failure-points-between-5m-and-100m-in-arr\/\">reflected on key mistakes<\/a> they made while leading the company to $100 million in annual recurring revenue, offering insights to help other founders avoid similar pitfalls.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Setting the stage for a battery gold rush:<\/strong>\u00a0Volkswagen&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/06\/20\/volkswagens-battery-lithium-ion-breakthrough\/\">breakthrough in lithium-ion battery technology<\/a> could significantly impact the automotive industry, especially as it grapples with increased costs due to inflation and supply chain issues.<\/p>\n<p><strong>F you, pay me:<\/strong>\u00a0If an investor tells you not to take a salary after you\u2019ve raised VC funding, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/09\/f-you-pay-me\/\">tell them to go do something anatomically strenuous<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>The best laid plans of mice and men:<\/strong> We examine the evolution of fintech over the past decade, looking on <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/02\/13\/a-decade-of-fintech-failures-4-innovations-that-didnt-live-up-to-the-hype\/\">several hyped fintech ideas that ultimately failed to transform<\/a> the financial services industry as intended.<\/p>\n<p><strong>To remote or not to remote:<\/strong> We looked at the shift in remote work startups, where initial <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/03\/remote-work-startups-future\">enthusiasm for dedicated remote work tools has waned<\/a>, as companies have adapted to a hybrid work model rather than a purely remote one, leading to challenges for startups focused solely on remote work solutions.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Here\u2019s why your pitch deck sucks:<\/strong> In the year of AI, I built a tool that analyzes startup pitch decks (because of course I did \u2014 why <em>wouldn\u2019t<\/em> I build a tool that puts me out of business) and found <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/12\/13\/fix-your-pitch-deck\">a ton of interesting data about what startup founders get wrong<\/a> when they create pitch decks.<\/p>\n<p>Oh, and because I just <em>know<\/em> you are crazy curious: The featured image of this post was taken with an iPhone 14 Pro Max. I created the bauble using the <a href=\"https:\/\/cuttle.xyz\/@cuttle\/Circular-Name-Ornament-OvPMAq0AuSof\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Circular Name Ornament creator<\/a> from Cuttle Labs, along with a Glowforge Aura. After <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/25\/glowforge-aura\/\">I reviewed the entry-level laser cutter from Glowforge in July<\/a>, I decided that I just had to have one. Because, well, what kind of nerd would I be if I didn\u2019t set shit on fire on a semi-regular basis.<\/p>\n<p>Happy New Year \u2014 see y\u2019all in 2024!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Welcome to Startups Weekly. /best-budgeting-apps-for-individuals-startups-and-small-businesses\/","title":{"rendered":"Best budgeting apps for individuals, startups and small businesses"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As we head into the New Year, you might be interested in creating a budget for yourself or you may be looking for a new tool to help manage your startup or small business\u2019s budget. You may be looking to switch out your current budgeting app for a better one, or perhaps you&#8217;re someone who has traditionally relied on spreadsheets. Although spreadsheets can be a simple way to manage and track a budget, it could be worth checking out budgeting apps to save yourself some time and effort. We\u2019ve compiled two lists of apps that we think are great budgeting tools for individuals and startups.<\/p>\n<p>For individuals, a good budgeting app can help you save money by creating and sticking to a monthly budget. For startups and small businesses, a good budgeting app can help you understand your company\u2019s financial health and make informed decisions. Whichever way you go, the best budgeting app for you will depend on your individual or business needs, so we\u2019ve included a variety of apps to help you find one that works best for you.<\/p>\n<h1>Best apps for individuals<\/h1>\n<h2>Goodbudget<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646316\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646316\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646316\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the Goodbudget app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"709\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png 1482w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=300,208 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=768,532 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=680,471 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=1200,831 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/goodbudget-app.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646316\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Goodbudget<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/goodbudget.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Goodbudget<\/a> is a good app if you\u2019re a beginner and just getting started out with budgeting. It uses the envelope system, which is one of the original ways of managing money. Goodbudget helps ensure that you are never caught off-guard by a bill or sudden expense. Each month, you set aside money for things that you need, like groceries and gas. Once you have set aside money for your essentials, you can then choose how to use the rest based on what\u2019s important to you.<\/p>\n<p>The app is also a great option if you have a shared household, as it lets you sync your budget with another person. Goodbudget offers both a free version and a paid version, which costs $8 per month. The free version includes everything you need to manage a budget, while the paid version gives you additional capabilities, such as email support, unlimited envelopes and the ability to use the service on five devices versus just two. One possible downside is that you have to manually enter your transactions in the app, as the app doesn\u2019t connect to your bank account.<\/p>\n<h2>PocketGuard<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646318\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646318\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646318\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the PocketGuard app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"712\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png 1660w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=300,209 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=768,534 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=680,473 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=1536,1068 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=1200,834 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/pocketguard-app.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646318\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> PocketGuard<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>If your main goal is to track your spending, <a href=\"https:\/\/pocketguard.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">PocketGuard<\/a> might be the best app for you. PocketGuard shows you how much spendable money you have after you set aside enough for your bills, goals and necessities. The app shows you a pie chart so you can visualize which expenses are taking up the most money. You can set spending limits in the app to make sure you\u2019re not spending beyond your means.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>PocketGuard links your banks, credit cards, loans and investments in one place in order to help you keep track of your account balances, net worth and more. There\u2019s a limited free version of the app and a paid version, which costs $8 per month and unlocks features like the ability to create your own spending categories, set a debt payoff plan, attach receipts, export transaction data and more.<\/p>\n<h2>Honeydue<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646319\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646319\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646319\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the Honeydue app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"715\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png 1790w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=150,105 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=300,209 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=768,536 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=680,475 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=1536,1073 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=1200,838 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/honeydue-app.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646319\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Honeydue<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.honeydue.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Honeydue<\/a> is a good budgeting app if you want to plan and manage your finances with your partner. The app syncs to yours and your partner\u2019s bank accounts. Honeydue lets you manage your money together while tracking your expenses and communicating about bills. You can chat with your partner in the app and decide whether one person will be covering a bill, or if the two of you will be splitting it evenly.<\/p>\n<p>The app also offers its own joint bank account. Honeydue is free to use, so it\u2019s a good option for couples who don\u2019t want to pay a monthly subscription. One downside is that there isn\u2019t a desktop version of the app, so if you\u2019re someone who likes to manage your finances on a bigger screen, Honeydue might not be the best option for you.<\/p>\n<h2>Empower<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646323\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646323\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646323\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png\" alt=\"The empower app on two mobile phones\" width=\"1024\" height=\"706\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png 1994w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=150,103 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=300,207 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=768,529 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=680,469 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=1536,1058 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=1200,827 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/empower-app.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646323\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Empower<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.empower.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Empower<\/a> is a good app if you want a tool for both budgeting and investing. The app lets you track all your accounts, including your bank and credit cards, IRAs, 401(k)s, mortgages and loans in one place. You can plan for retirement, monitor your investments and uncover hidden fees. Empower features a money-tracking dashboard that lets you track your expenses based on categories.<\/p>\n<p>The service is free to use and is designed to help you manage both your day-to-day finances while also helping plan for the future. However, if your main goal is to budget your spending, Empower might not be the best option for you. You may be better off choosing a different app on this list because Empower\u2019s budgeting tools aren\u2019t as advanced as some of the other ones.<\/p>\n<h1>Best apps for startups and small businesses<\/h1>\n<h2>FreshBooks<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646326\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646326\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646326\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the Freshbooks app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"707\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png 1874w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=300,207 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=768,530 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=680,470 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=1536,1061 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=1200,829 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/freshbooks-app.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646326\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> FreshBooks<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.freshbooks.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">FreshBooks<\/a> is a simple tool that can help startups and small businesses create a budget and stick to it. The service connects to your bank account or credit card to track your expenses. FreshBooks has tools for invoicing, time tracking, bookkeeping, payments and more. It lets you take receipt photos, forward email receipts to your account and import expenses from your bank account.<\/p>\n<p>The service has tools for businesses at all stages, from freelancers to businesses with multiple employees. FreshBooks allows your team, clients and contractors to collaborate and share files and updates in one place. It can also integrate with over 100 apps including Dropbox, HubSpot, GSuite, Stripe and more. FreshBooks has four pricing tiers, with its business ones starting at $30 per month.<\/p>\n<h2>QuickBooks<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646329\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646329\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646329\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the QuickBooks app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"702\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png 2060w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=150,103 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=300,206 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=768,526 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=680,466 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=1536,1053 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=2048,1404 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=1200,823 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/quickbooks-app.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646329\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> QuickBooks<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/quickbooks.intuit.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">QuickBooks<\/a> is a simple service that helps you get a full overview of your business\u2019s finances by tracking your business expenses, income, profitability, taxes and more. The service helps you not only budget, but also manage the accounting tasks that are associated with your startup or business. You can see profit at a glance, pay your team, manage your money, accept payments and track and manage your time.<\/p>\n<p>The service features an easy-to-navigate dashboard that lets you easily understand your business\u2019s financial health. QuickBooks also offers tax preparation features, and gives you the ability to consult with experts to help you get ready for tax time. QuickBooks has three pricing tiers starting at $30 per month.<\/p>\n<h2>Toshl<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646333\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646333\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646333\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the Toshl app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"710\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png 1812w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=300,208 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=768,532 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=680,471 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=1536,1065 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=1200,832 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/toshl-app.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646333\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Toshl<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>If you want a reasonably priced and simple, but effective, budgeting tool, <a href=\"https:\/\/toshl.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Toshl<\/a> may be the app for you. Although it\u2019s marketed as a personal budgeting app, Toshl can be a good tool for new startups looking to understand and manage their finances for a fraction of the cost of budgeting apps marketed toward small businesses.<\/p>\n<p>Toshl features a user-friendly intuitive experience that lets you create a budget and track expenses. If you want to budget for something in particular, you can set the budget to track only expenses with particular categories, tags or financial accounts. Budgets can be set monthly, weekly, daily or for a custom period of your choosing. The service has a free version and a paid version that costs $4.99 per month.<\/p>\n<h2>Xero<\/h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2646334\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img decoding=\"async\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2646334\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2646334\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png\" alt=\"Three screenshots of the Xero app\" width=\"1024\" height=\"706\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png 1892w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=150,103 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=300,207 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=768,529 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=680,469 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=1536,1059 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=1200,827 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/12\/xero-app.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2646334\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Xero<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.xero.com\/us\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Xero<\/a> is a good budgeting and finance tool for businesses and startups that are ready for growth. The service\u2019s Budget Manager worksheet lets you create an overall budget for each of your tracking categories. There are also other tools that let you see short-term cash flow and business snapshots.<\/p>\n<p>You can use Xero to send invoices and quotes, pay bills, track projects, manage expenses, accept payments and more. Xero is designed to help small businesses make decisions using trend analysis and simple reporting. In addition to financial features, Xero includes features that help with inventory and project management. The service offers three paid tiers, starting at $15 per month.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>As we head into the New Year, you might be interested in creating a budget for yourself or you may be looking for a new tool to help manage your startup or small business\u2019s budget. bis-market-germany\/","title":{"rendered":"With hopes for greener grass in Germany vanishing, consolidation is in the cards for cannabis companies"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">As 2023 comes<\/span> to an end, it is only natural to reflect on what happened in the markets we cover. But when it comes to cannabis, the answer is \u201cnot much,\u201d which won&#8217;t help cannabis startups that are already facing a challenging funding environment.<\/p>\n<p>Namely, 2023 wasn&#8217;t the year that Germany legalized adult recreational cannabis use. That matters because that&#8217;s not what the legal cannabis market once anticipated, and whenever there is misalignment between reality and what investors expected, especially when public companies boosted said <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ft.com\/content\/9eab3125-8c7a-4e9c-8ef5-50fb8dae1965\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expectations<\/a>, it is rarely good news. Or at least, not for everyone.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;One trend to look out for in 2024 is consolidation,&#8221; said cannabis-focused investor Matt Hawkins, a managing principal at specialized VC firm Entourage Effect Capital. &#8220;Companies have spent significant capital in preparation for a sizable commercial market in Germany. [As] the chances of that happening fade, companies might not be able to support their operations without joining forces.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s take a look at what to remember from 2023 and what to expect in 2024, with help from a brand-new <a href=\"https:\/\/prohibitionpartners.com\/reports\/the-global-cannabis-report-4th-edition\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">global cannabis report<\/a> from market intelligence firm Prohibition Partners.<\/p>\n<h2>What didn&#8217;t happen<\/h2>\n<p>The expectations that the EU&#8217;s most populated country might legalize recreational marijuana didn&#8217;t come out of thin air; this possibility was very much on the table ever since a <a href=\"https:\/\/en.wikipedia.org\/wiki\/Traffic_light_coalition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">traffic light coalition<\/a> took power in Germany in December 2021. But this coalition of social democrats, liberals and greens watered down its plans so much since then that one has to wonder how well prepared it was to overcome legal challenges that shouldn&#8217;t have come as a surprise.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Not much happened when it comes to legal cannabis markets in 2023, which is launching two new subscription tiers, including a &#8216;Premium+&#8217; ad-free plan"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">X, formerly known as Twitter, is introducing <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/premium\/status\/1717977644996644948\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">two new tiers<\/a> for its subscription offering in order to bring in additional revenue. The social media giant is adding a new Premium+ tier that costs $16 per month and offers the &#8220;largest reply boost&#8221; and removes ads from the For You and Following feeds. The tier also comes with revenue-sharing, along with access to other creator tools.<\/p>\n<p>The second tier launching today is called &#8220;Basic&#8221; and costs $3 per month. The tier doesn&#8217;t come with a blue checkmark, but includes basic features like the ability to edit posts and post longer text and videos. It also offers a &#8220;small reply boost.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--twitter\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">introducing Premium+<\/p>\n<p>\u2013 no ads in For You or Following<br \/>\u2013 largest boost for your replies (vs other Premium tiers or unverified users)<br \/>\u2013 access to our full suite of creator tools<\/p>\n<p>now available on Web \u270c\ufe0f <\/p>\n<p>subscribe here \u2192\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/Ywvyijo9CQ\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https:\/\/t.co\/Ywvyijo9CQ<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Premium (@premium) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/premium\/status\/1717977644996644948?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">October 27, 2023<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Both of the new tiers are now available on the web.<\/p>\n<p>The new tiers join the standard X Premium tier, which replaced Twitter Blue. The tier costs $8 per month and gives users a blue checkmark, prioritized ranking in replies, bookmark folders, longer posts, text formatting, themes, sms two-factor authentication, encrypted DMs and more.<\/p>\n<p>The launch of the new tiers comes<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/06\/x-to-test-three-tiers-of-its-premium-service-ceo-says-code-shows-one-tier-may-be-ad-free\/\"> a few weeks<\/a> after <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2023-10-05\/x-tells-bankers-that-advertisers-are-back-but-spending-less?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg<\/a> reported that X was working on new subscription tiers.<\/p>\n<p>The introduction of the new tiers will give X additional ways to grow revenues as it deals with the loss in advertising dollars that it has faced since Elon Musk took the reins of the platform last fall. Musk&#8217;s controversial changes have turned away advertisers, as major companies ended up pulling their ads from the social network after their ads were displayed next to hate speech <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/08\/17\/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/08\/17\/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups\/\">and pro-Nazi content.<\/a> Earlier this month, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04\/\">Reuters<\/a> reported that the company&#8217;s U.S. ad revenue has declined every month since Musk took over, with the latest figures showing a 60% year-over-year decline as of August.<\/p>\n<p>Since taking over the company last year, Musk has been looking for ways to generate additional revenue, and has gone so far as charging users in New Zealand and the Philippines <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/17\/x-starts-experimenting-with-a-1-per-year-fee-for-new-users\">$1 per year<\/a> in order to access the social network.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"w3xp4u7QHX\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/27\/a-year-after-musks-takeover-x-says-an-average-user-spends-32-minutes-per-day-on-the-platform\/\">A year after Musk&#8217;s takeover, X says an average user spends 32 minutes per day on the platform<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute;
